8 min
The Intra-Hanafi Dispute for Unspecified Property
Presents Al-Karkhi's four scenarios and the mashayikh's absolute prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Al-Karkhi's four scenarios for unspecified usurped goods, the mashayikh's response, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
For unspecified goods, Al-Karkhi permits profit in three cases; the majority prohibits it entirely.

When usurped property is not specified by designation (like currency), the ruling becomes debated within the Hanafi school. Al-Karkhi proposed a four-scenario analysis, but the majority of later scholars (mashayikh) rejected his permissive views and maintained that profit from any usurped property must be given in charity. This lesson unpacks the dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property type
The scenario involves goods that do not become specified by designation (ghayr muta'ayyin), such as gold or silver coins.
This is the context for the dispute.
2
Al-Karkhi's four scenarios
Al-Karkhi divides based on pointing (ishara) and payment (naqd): 1) pointed + paid from it (profit not pure), 2) pointed + paid from others, 3) pointed to other + paid from it, 4) absolute pointing + paid from it (all three profit pure).
The first scenario is the only one where profit is not pure.
3
Mashayikh's response
The majority of our scholars (mashayikh) hold that profit is never pure in any case, regardless of the pointing or payment. This is the chosen view (mukhtar).
They argue that the pointing creates a doubt of prohibition due to the unlawful origin.
4
Note the tarjih
The mashayikh view is preferred, though some later scholars choose Al-Karkhi's fatwa due to widespread unlawful transactions.
This is a concession for necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الغصب. الله تعالى : الثاني وهو ما إذا تصرف في المغصوب أو الوديعة وربح فهو على وجوه: إما أن يكون مما يتعين بالتعيين كالعرض أو لا يتعين كالنقدين، فإن كان مما يتعين لا يحل له التناول منه قبل ضمان القيمة وبعده يحل إلا فيما زاد على قدر القيمة وهو الربح المذكور هنا فإنه لا يطيب له ويتصدق به لأن العقد يتعلق فيما لا يتعين بالعتيين حتى تنفسخ بالهلاك قبل القبض فتمكن الخبث فيه. وإن كان مما لا يتعين فقد قال الكرخي : إنه على أربعة أوجه : إما إن أشار ونقد منه أو أشار إليه ونقد من غيره أو أشار إلى غيره ونقد منه أو أطلق إطلاقاً ونقد منه، وفي كل ذلك يطيب له إلا في الوجه الأول وهو ما إذا أشار إليه ونقد منه لأن الإشارة إليه لا تفيد التعيين فيستوي وجودها وعدمها إلا إذا تأكدت بالنقد منهما. وقال مشايخنا رحمهم أنه لا يطيب له بكل حال وهو المختار وإطلاق الجواب في الجامعين يدل على ذلك. ووجهه بالنقد منه استفاد سلامة المشتري وبالإشارة استفاد جواز العقد لتعلق العقد في حق الوصف والقدر فيثبت فيه شبهة لحرمة لمالكه بسبب خبيث واختار بعضهم الفتوى على قول الكرخي في زماننا لكثرة الحرام. وهذا كله على قولهما، وعند أبي يوسف لا يتصدق بشيء منه والوجه ما بينا. وهذا الاختلاف منهم فيما إذا صار بالتقلب من جنس ما ضمن بأن غصب مثلاً وصار في يده من ثمن المغصوب دراهم كان في يده من بدله بخلاف جنس ما دراهم ضمن بأن غصب دراهم وفي يده من بدله طعام أو عروض لا يجب عليه التصدق بالإجماع لأن الربح إنما يتعين عند اتحاد الجنس وما لم يصر بالتقلب من جنس ما ضمن لا يظهر الربح ولو اشترى بثمن المبيع بيعاً فاسداً شيئاً وأشار إليه ونقد منه يطيب الربح لأن الثمن صار ملكاً بالقبض بتراضيهما، ولأنه متى نقض البيع واسترد الثمن يرد مثل الثمن لا عينه ولكن هذا لا يوجب بينهم الخبث في التصرف للحال ولو اشترى بالدراهم المغصوبة طعاماً حل التناول، ولو اشترى بالدراهم المغصوبة دنانير لم يجز له أن يتصرف في الدنانير لأن الدراهم لو استحقت بعد ما افترقا انتقض البيع في الدنانير فوجب عليها ردها، فأما البيع في الطعام لا ينقض باستحقاق الدراهم لأنه يجب عليه رد مثلها لا عينها. ولو اشترى بالثوب المغصوب جارية يحرم عليه أن يطأها حتى يدفع قيمة الثوب إلى صاحبه لأن بالاستحقاق تبين أن البيع فاسد لأن البيع يتعلق بعين الثوب . ولو اشترى بالدراهم المغصوبة جارية حل له وطؤها لأن البيع لا يتعين بتلك الدراهم، ولو تزوج بالثوب المغصوب جارية امرأة حل له وطؤها لأن النكاح لا ينتقض باستحقاق المهر، ولو أخذ المالك القيمة بقول الغاصب في الجارية المغصوبة لم يحل له وطؤها واستخدامها ولا بيعها إلا إذا أعطاه قيمتها بتمامها لأنها من غير رضا المالك، ولهذا لا يملك الفسخ إن ظهر مستحقة. ولو اعتق الغاصب العبد بعد القضاء عليه بالقيمة الناقصة جاز عنده وعليه تمام القيمة ; كذا في المحيط مختصراً.
Book of Usurpation. Key Terms
إشارة (ishara): Pointing to the specific property in a contract; it does not effect specification for fungibles.
نقد (naqd): Payment from the specific usurped property.

According to the mashayikh, when is profit from unspecified usurped property pure?
A) In all cases
B) In three of four scenarios
C) In none of the cases
D) Only when payment is from other funds

Key Takeaway

Practical Cases: Applying the Rulings on Profit from Usurped Property
Lists multiple practical cases illustrating the application of the above principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings to various scenarios: buying food, slave-girl, marriage, and dealing with owner's claim.

Core Idea
The ruling on profit varies with property type, same-type transformation, and the nature of the subsequent transaction.

The passage concludes with a series of practical cases that apply the principles discussed. These cases illustrate how the distinction between specified and unspecified property, and the condition of same-type transformation, affect the rulings on profit and the validity of subsequent transactions. This lesson walks through each case to solidify understanding.

Guided Path
1
Understand the same-type condition
The dispute about charity only applies when the usurped property has been transformed into the same type (e.g., usurped item sold for dirhams, and dirhams are the substitute). If the type differs (e.g., dirhams turned into food), there is consensus that no charity is required.
Profit only appears when types are the same.
2
Case: buying food with usurped dirhams
If the usurper buys food with usurped dirhams, the food is lawful to consume. Reason: the dirhams are fungible, and the contract is valid from the buyer's perspective.
No charity required because the type changed.
3
Case: buying dinars with usurped dirhams
Buying dinars with usurped dirhams is not valid; the dinars must be returned because the sale can be rescinded if the dirhams are claimed.
The sale of dinars is rescindable because it is a barter of the same genus (currency).
4
Case: buying a slave-girl with usurped garment
Intercourse is forbidden until the value of the garment is paid to the owner, because the garment is specified and the sale is void upon claim.
The contract attaches to the specific garment.
5
Case: marriage with usurped dower
Marriage with a usurped garment as dower is valid; intercourse is lawful because marriage is not rescinded by the claim of the dower.
The nikkah is robust; the dower is a debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الغصب. الله تعالى : الثاني وهو ما إذا تصرف في المغصوب أو الوديعة وربح فهو على وجوه: إما أن يكون مما يتعين بالتعيين كالعرض أو لا يتعين كالنقدين، فإن كان مما يتعين لا يحل له التناول منه قبل ضمان القيمة وبعده يحل إلا فيما زاد على قدر القيمة وهو الربح المذكور هنا فإنه لا يطيب له ويتصدق به لأن العقد يتعلق فيما لا يتعين بالعتيين حتى تنفسخ بالهلاك قبل القبض فتمكن الخبث فيه. وإن كان مما لا يتعين فقد قال الكرخي : إنه على أربعة أوجه : إما إن أشار ونقد منه أو أشار إليه ونقد من غيره أو أشار إلى غيره ونقد منه أو أطلق إطلاقاً ونقد منه، وفي كل ذلك يطيب له إلا في الوجه الأول وهو ما إذا أشار إليه ونقد منه لأن الإشارة إليه لا تفيد التعيين فيستوي وجودها وعدمها إلا إذا تأكدت بالنقد منهما. وقال مشايخنا رحمهم أنه لا يطيب له بكل حال وهو المختار وإطلاق الجواب في الجامعين يدل على ذلك. ووجهه بالنقد منه استفاد سلامة المشتري وبالإشارة استفاد جواز العقد لتعلق العقد في حق الوصف والقدر فيثبت فيه شبهة لحرمة لمالكه بسبب خبيث واختار بعضهم الفتوى على قول الكرخي في زماننا لكثرة الحرام. وهذا كله على قولهما، وعند أبي يوسف لا يتصدق بشيء منه والوجه ما بينا. وهذا الاختلاف منهم فيما إذا صار بالتقلب من جنس ما ضمن بأن غصب مثلاً وصار في يده من ثمن المغصوب دراهم كان في يده من بدله بخلاف جنس ما دراهم ضمن بأن غصب دراهم وفي يده من بدله طعام أو عروض لا يجب عليه التصدق بالإجماع لأن الربح إنما يتعين عند اتحاد الجنس وما لم يصر بالتقلب من جنس ما ضمن لا يظهر الربح ولو اشترى بثمن المبيع بيعاً فاسداً شيئاً وأشار إليه ونقد منه يطيب الربح لأن الثمن صار ملكاً بالقبض بتراضيهما، ولأنه متى نقض البيع واسترد الثمن يرد مثل الثمن لا عينه ولكن هذا لا يوجب بينهم الخبث في التصرف للحال ولو اشترى بالدراهم المغصوبة طعاماً حل التناول، ولو اشترى بالدراهم المغصوبة دنانير لم يجز له أن يتصرف في الدنانير لأن الدراهم لو استحقت بعد ما افترقا انتقض البيع في الدنانير فوجب عليها ردها، فأما البيع في الطعام لا ينقض باستحقاق الدراهم لأنه يجب عليه رد مثلها لا عينها. ولو اشترى بالثوب المغصوب جارية يحرم عليه أن يطأها حتى يدفع قيمة الثوب إلى صاحبه لأن بالاستحقاق تبين أن البيع فاسد لأن البيع يتعلق بعين الثوب . ولو اشترى بالدراهم المغصوبة جارية حل له وطؤها لأن البيع لا يتعين بتلك الدراهم، ولو تزوج بالثوب المغصوب جارية امرأة حل له وطؤها لأن النكاح لا ينتقض باستحقاق المهر، ولو أخذ المالك القيمة بقول الغاصب في الجارية المغصوبة لم يحل له وطؤها واستخدامها ولا بيعها إلا إذا أعطاه قيمتها بتمامها لأنها من غير رضا المالك، ولهذا لا يملك الفسخ إن ظهر مستحقة. ولو اعتق الغاصب العبد بعد القضاء عليه بالقيمة الناقصة جاز عنده وعليه تمام القيمة ; كذا في المحيط مختصراً.
Book of Usurpation. Allah the Exalted: The second is when he transacts in the usurped or trust and makes a profit, then it is in several ways: Either it is something that becomes specified by designation like a commodity, or not specified like the two coin types (gold/silver). If it is that which becomes specified, it is not lawful for him to take from it before guaranteeing the value, and after that it is lawful, except what exceeds the amount of the value, which is the profit mentioned here; then it is not pure for him and he must give it in charity, because the contract, in what is not specified, attaches to the two things until it is dissolved by destruction before receipt, so corruption becomes established in it. And if it is that which is not specified, then Al-Karkhi said: it is in four ways: either he pointed to it and paid from it, or he pointed to it and paid from other than it, or he pointed to other than it and paid from it, or he made an absolute (pointing) and paid from it. In all of that it is pure for him except the first way, which is when he pointed to it and paid from it, because pointing to it does not effect specification, so its presence and absence are equal, unless it is confirmed by paying from both. And our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) said: it is not pure for him in any case, and that is the chosen position, and the absolute answer in the two Jami's indicates that. And its reasoning: by paying from it, he obtained safety for the buyer, and by pointing, he obtained permissibility of the contract, because the contract attaches with respect to description and amount, so a doubt of prohibition for its owner due to evil is established. And some chose the fatwa according to Al-Karkhi's statement in our time due to the abundance of unlawful. And all this is according to their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) statement. According to Abu Yusuf, he does not give anything in charity from it, and the opinion is as we explained. And this difference among them is when the property has by transformation become of the same type as what he guaranteed, e.g., he usurped an item and in his hand from the price of the usurped item there are dirhams that are from its substitute, as opposed to if it became of a different type from the dirhams he guaranteed, e.g., he usurped dirhams and in his hand from their substitute there is food or commodities: he is not obligated to give in charity by consensus, because profit is only determined when the type is the same, and as long as it has not by transformation become of the same type as what he guaranteed, the profit does not appear. And if he buys something with the price of a void sale, pointing to it and paying from it, the profit is pure because the price became ownership by receipt with mutual consent, and because when he cancels the sale and reclaims the price, he returns the equivalent of the price, not its exact item, but this does not necessitate evil in the transaction for the present. And if he buys food with usurped dirhams, it is lawful to consume. And if he buys dinars with usurped dirhams, it is not permissible for him to transact in the dinars because if the dirhams are claimed as rightfully owned after they separated, the sale of the dinars is rescinded, so he must return them. As for the sale of food, it is not rescinded by the claim of the dirhams because he must return their equivalent, not their exact items. And if he buys a slave-girl with the usurped garment, it is forbidden for him to have intercourse with her until he pays the value of the garment to its owner, because by the claim it becomes clear that the sale is void, since the sale attaches to the exact garment. And if he buys a slave-girl with usurped dirhams, it is lawful for him to have intercourse with her because the sale is not specified by those dirhams. And if he marries a woman with the usurped garment as dower, it is lawful for him to have intercourse with her because marriage is not rescinded by the claim of the dower. And if the owner takes the value based on the statement of the usurper regarding the usurped slave-girl, it is not lawful for him to have intercourse with her, use her for service, or sell her, unless he gives her full value, because it is without the owner's consent; for this reason, he does not have the option of rescission if it appears that she was rightfully owned by another. And if the usurper emancipates the slave after being ordered to pay the deficient value, it is valid according to him (Abu Hanifa), and he owes the full value; thus in Al-Muhit, abridged.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Usurpation (Kitab al-Ghasb) in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the ruling on profit (ribh) when a usurper or trustee transacts with usurped or trust property and makes a gain. The passage is an expansion probe, building on the base text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author first distinguishes between property that is 'specified by designation' (muta'ayyin) like a commodity, and property that is not specified like currency (gold and silver coins). For specified property, any profit above the value is not lawful for the usurper and must be given in charity, because the contract attaches to the specific item, and after destruction before receipt, the contract dissolves, leaving a taint (khubth). For unspecified property, the author presents the view of Al-Karkhi, who divides the transaction into four scenarios based on whether the usurper pointed to the property and paid from it or not; in all but one scenario the profit is lawful. However, the majority of our scholars (mashayikh) hold that it is never lawful and must be given in charity; this is the chosen (mukhtar) view. The reason is that the usurper's action combines paying (which secures the buyer's safety) and pointing (which makes the contract permissible but creates a doubt due to the unlawful origin). Some latter scholars preferred Al-Karkhi's fatwa in their time due to widespread unlawful transactions. The passage then notes that this ruling applies according to the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf holds that no charity is required at all. The difference is confined to cases where the usurped property has been transformed into the same type as the guarantee (e.g., the usurper obtains dirhams from selling the usurped item). If the type differs (e.g., usurped dirhams turned into food), there is consensus that no charity is required because profit only appears when types are the same. The passage then gives multiple illustrative cases: buying food with usurped dirhams is lawful; buying dinars is not lawful because the sale can be rescinded; buying a slave-girl with a usurped garment forbids intercourse until the value is paid, while with dirhams it is lawful; marriage with usurped dower does not invalidate the marriage; if the owner takes the value based on the usurper's statement, he cannot use the slave-girl until he receives full value; and emancipation by the usurper after partial payment is valid but he owes the full value.

Key Terms
تقلب (taqallub): Transformation of usurped property into another type through sale or exchange.
جنس (jins): Type or genus; e.g., currency, food, commodities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on buying food with usurped dirhams?
A) The food is unlawful to consume.
B) The food is lawful to consume.
C) The food must be returned to the usurper.
D) The food must be given in charity.

Key Takeaway
The practical application of the profit ruling depends crucially on property specification, same-type transformation, and the nature of the contract (sale vs. marriage).

Ownership of Transformed Usurped Property: The Hanafi Dabit and the Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute with regulation of property transformation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ownership of transformed usurped property, identify the three conditions of the dabit, and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Transformation by the usurper transfers ownership, but use is forbidden until payment — to prevent injustice and usurpation.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a critical issue in ghasb: when a usurper changes the usurped item so thoroughly that it becomes a new thing. The Hanafi school, relying on istihsan and a hadith, holds that ownership shifts to the usurper, but with a crucial restriction: he cannot use it until he compensates the original owner. This lesson unpacks the controlling principle (al-dabit) and the debate with Imam al-Shafi'i over whether the usurper ever becomes owner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its formula
Read the base text statement: '(And he owns it without lawful use before paying the substitute)'. Note that ownership is established but use is conditional on payment.
The formula shows both the transfer and the restriction.
2
Extract the three conditions of the dabit
Find the phrase: 'whenever the usurped item is changed by action until its name is removed and its benefits increase and it mixes with the usurper's property so that it cannot be distinguished at all.' List the three conditions: (1) name removed, (2) benefits increase, (3) mixing prevents distinction.
All three must be present for ownership to transfer.
3
Note exceptions and non-acting transformation
Identify the exceptions: gold and silver are not owned by making into vessels/coins. Also, if transformation occurs naturally (grapes to raisins), ownership does not transfer; owner may choose to take or claim value.
The usurper's act is crucial (bi fi'lihi).
4
Compare Hanafi and Shafi'i positions
The text presents Imam al-Shafi'i's view that the owner's right never ceases. Contrast with the Hanafi view that ownership transfers under the dabit. Note the narration from Abu Yusuf supporting Shafi'i.
This is the core ikhtilaf of the lesson.
5
Evaluate the evidence
Examine the Hanafi proof: the hadith of the slaughtered sheep ('Feed it to the captives') shows the Prophet recognized ownership. Also, the analogy of prayer in usurped land (a prohibited act can cause reward). Understand istihsan overriding qiyas.
Istihsan is used to forbid use until payment, preventing abuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الغصب. قال رحمه الله : :(وملك بلا حل انتفاع قبل أداء الضمان بطحن وطبخ وشي وزرع واتخاذ سيف أو أناء لغير الحجرين لأنه لو لم يملكه بذلك لحقه ضرر وكان ظلماً والظالم لا يظلم بل ينصف. ثم الضابط فيه أنه متى تغيرت العين المغصوبة بفعل حتى زال اسمها وعظم منافعها واختلطت بملك الغاصب حتى لا يمكن تميزها أصلاً زال ملك المغصوب منه وملكها الغاصب وضمنها ولا يحل له الانتفاع بها حتى يؤدي بدلها قال في العناية وغيرها : وقوله بطحن إلى آخره يعني بفعل الغاصب احترازاً عما إذا تغير بغير فعله مثل إن صار العنب زبيباً بنفسه أو خلاً أو الرطب تمراً فإن الغاصب لا يملكه والمالك فيه بالخيار إن شاء أخذه وإن شاء تركه وضمنه مثله. وقوله زال اسمها يحترز عما إذا لم يزل اسمها كما لو ذبح الشاة فإنه يقال شاة حية وشاة مذبوحة. وقوله عظم منافعها تأكيد يتناول الحنطة إذا طحنها فإنه يزول بالطحن عظم منافعها كجعلها هريسة وكشكاً ونشاء وغير ذلك. قال صاحب العناية : وقوله وعظم منافعها تأكيد لقوله زال اسمها والظاهر أنه تأسيس لا تأكيد لأنه احتراز عما إذا غصب شاة وذبحها فإنه لا يزول بالذبح ملك مالكها كما سيأتي مصرحاً به، وما ذكره ره من الطحن وما بعده يحصل به ما ذكرنا في الضابط فيملكها الغاصب إلا الذهب والفضة فإنه لا يملكه باتخاذهما أواني أو دراهم أو دنانير عند الإمام لأنها بهذا الفعل لا يزول التمييز. وقال الإمام الشافعي : لا ينقطع حق المالك بما ذكر وهي رواية عن أبي يوسف غير أنه إذا أختار أخذ العين لا يضمن النقصان في الربويات لأن الملك نعمة فلا يحصل بالحرام وهو الغصب وصار كما وقعت الحنطة في الطاحونة وانطحنت بفعل الماء أو الهواء من غير صنع أحد. ولنا ان لما استهلك العين من وجه بالاستحالة حتى صار له اسم آخر وقد أحدث وهي حق الغا سب وهي قائمة من كل وجه فترجحت لذلك والمحظور لغيره لا يمتنع أن يكون سبباً لحكم شرعي ألا ترى أن الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة لا تجوز وتكون سبباً لحصول الثواب ا زيل فما ظنك بالملك غير أنه لا يجوز له الانتفاع بها قبل الأداء لا ينفتح باب الغصب ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في الشاة المذبوحة بغير إذن مالكها «أطعموها الأسارى ولو لم يملكه لما قال ذلك والقياس أنه يجوز الانتفاع به وهو قول الحسن زفر ورواية عن أبي حنيفة ولهذا ينفذ تصرفه فيها كالتمليك للغير. ووجه الاستحسان ما ذكرناه ونفاذ تصرفه لوجود الملك ألا ترى أن المشتري شراء فاسداً ينفذ تصرفه فيه مع أنه لا يحل له الانتفاع به. فإذا دفع المثل أو القيمة إليه وأخذه بحكم الحاكم أو تراضيا على مقدار حل الانتفاع به لوجود الرضا من المغصوب منه لأن الحاكم لا يحكم إلا بطلبه فحصلت المبادلة بالتراضي. وقال أبو يوسف في الحنطة المزروعة والنواة المزروعة يجوز الانتفاع بها قبل أداء الضمان لوجود الاستهلاك من كل وجه . وقيد بقوله واتخاذ سيف ليفيد أنه بعده صار يباع فيه الصنعة
Book of Usurpation. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: "And he owns it without lawful use before paying the substitute by grinding, cooking, roasting, planting, and making a sword or a vessel for other than the two stones (gold and silver), because if he did not own it by that, harm would befall him and it would be injustice, and the wrongdoer is not treated unjustly but rather equity is done." Then the controlling principle: whenever the usurped item is changed by action until its name is removed and its benefits increase and it mixes with the usurper's property so that it cannot be distinguished at all, the ownership of the usurpee ceases and the usurper owns it and is liable for it, and it is not lawful for him to benefit from it until he pays its substitute. He said in Al-`Inayah and others: his statement "by grinding" etc. means by the action of the usurper, as a precaution against when it changes without his action, like if the grapes become raisins by themselves or vinegar, or fresh dates become dry dates: then the usurper does not own it, and the owner has the choice: if he wishes he may take it, and if he wishes he may leave it and its like is guaranteed. And his statement "its name is removed" is a precaution against when its name is not removed, like when he slaughters a sheep, for it is said 'live sheep' and 'slaughtered sheep'. And his statement "its benefits increase" is a confirmation that includes wheat when he grinds it, for by grinding its great benefits are removed, like making it into porridge, kashk, starch, etc. The author of Al-`Inayah said: and his statement "and its benefits increase" is a confirmation of his statement "its name is removed", and the apparent is that it is an establishment (ta'sis), not a confirmation, because it is a precaution against when he usurps a sheep and slaughters it: then slaughter does not remove the owner's ownership, as will be explicitly stated. And what he (the author) mentioned of grinding and after that achieves what we mentioned in the control: the usurper owns it, except gold and silver, for he does not own them by making them into vessels or coins according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) because by this action the distinctiveness is not removed. And Imam Al-Shafi'i said: the owner's right is not cut off by what was mentioned, and there is a narration from Abu Yusuf. However, if he chooses to take the item, he does not guarantee the deficiency in ribawi items, because ownership is a blessing, so it is not obtained by the unlawful (usurpation), and it becomes like wheat that fell into a mill and was ground by the action of water or wind without anyone's doing. And our proof: since he has consumed the item in one aspect by transformation until it has another name, and he has created something new, and it is the right of the usurper, and it exists in every aspect, so it is preponderant due to that. And what is prohibited for other than him does not prevent it from being a cause for a legal ruling; do you not see that prayer in usurped land is not permissible yet it becomes a cause for obtaining reward if it is removed? So what do you think about ownership? However, it is not permissible for him to benefit from it before payment, so that the door of usurpation is not opened. And because of his statement, peace be upon him, regarding the sheep slaughtered without the permission of its owner: 'Feed it to the captives'; if he did not own it, he would not have said that. And the analogy (qiyas) is that it is permissible to benefit from it, and that is the statement of Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and a narration from Abu Hanifa. For this reason, his disposal in it is effective, like giving ownership to another. And the basis of istihsan is what we mentioned, and the effectiveness of his disposal is due to the existence of ownership; do you not see that the buyer in a void sale has effective disposal in it even though it is not lawful for him to benefit from it? So when he pays the equivalent or the value to him and takes it by the ruling of a judge or they mutually agree on an amount, then benefiting from it becomes lawful due to the existence of consent from the usurpee, because the judge only rules upon his request, so an exchange by mutual consent occurs. And Abu Yusuf said regarding sown wheat and the planted date pit: it is permissible to benefit from them before paying the substitute, due to complete consumption in every aspect. And his restriction by saying "making a sword" indicates that after that, the craftsmanship becomes saleable in it.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the Hanafi ruling on when a usurper becomes the owner of usurped property that he has transformed. The base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states: 'And he owns it without lawful use before paying the substitute by grinding, cooking, roasting, planting, and making a sword or a vessel for other than the two stones (gold and silver).' The commentary then lays down the controlling principle (dabit): whenever the usurped item is changed by the usurper's act such that its name is removed, its benefits increase, and it becomes mixed with the usurper's property to the point that it cannot be distinguished, the original owner's ownership ceases and the usurper becomes owner, but he cannot use it until he pays the substitute (mithl or qimah). This principle is elaborated with caveats: changes not caused by the usurper (e.g., grapes becoming raisins on their own) do not transfer ownership; the owner may choose to take the item or leave it and claim its like. Slaughter of a sheep does not remove its name (it is still called a sheep), so ownership does not transfer; similarly, stoning does not change the name, so the owner remains owner. Grinding wheat removes its name (it becomes flour) and increases benefits (making various foodstuffs), so ownership transfers. Gold and silver are exceptions: making them into vessels or coins does not remove their distinctiveness, so according to Abu Hanifa, they are not owned by the usurper. The passage then presents the position of Imam Al-Shafi'i and a narration from Abu Yusuf that the owner's right does not cease at all. The Hanafi response is built on the principle that partial consumption through transformation gives the usurper a new creation and the item is now his in form, so he becomes owner, though use is barred until payment. The analogy of prayer in usurped land shows that a prohibited act can still be a cause for a legal effect (reward). A hadith about feeding a slaughtered sheep to captives is cited as proof that the usurper owns it, otherwise the Prophet would not have ordered that. The qiyas (analogy) would allow use without payment, but istihsan forbids use to prevent opening the door to usurpation. The passage also notes that the usurper's disposal in the item (e.g., giving it away) is effective despite the prohibition on use, just as a buyer in a void sale can dispose. Finally, Abu Yusuf allows use of planted wheat and date pits before payment due to complete consumption. The restriction to 'making a sword' in the base text indicates that after transformation, the craftsmanship becomes valuable and can be sold.

Key Terms
الضابط (al-dabit): The controlling principle or legal criterion that governs when a usurper becomes owner of transformed property.
استحالة (istihalah): Transformation of an item's essence, such that its name and properties change (e.g., grapes to raisins).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a usurper grinds usurped wheat into flour, what is the ruling?
A) The usurper does not own the flour; the owner may claim it.
B) The usurper owns the flour but cannot use it until he pays the value of the wheat.
C) The usurper owns the flour and may use it immediately.
D) The flour must be given in charity.

Key Takeaway
A usurper becomes owner of transformed property only if the name changes, benefits increase, and it becomes indistinguishable; even then, he cannot use it until he pays compensation.

The Dispute on Gold and Silver: Do They Pass to the Usurper?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ownership of gold/silver after transformation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's position on gold and silver after usurpation, explain his dalil, compare it with the Sahibayn's view, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Gold and silver retain their nature as price – the usurper does not own them even after transformation.

The general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that a usurper who transforms the usurped object (e.g., grinding wheat, roasting meat) becomes its owner, but cannot benefit from it until he pays the substitute (badal). However, an exception is made for gold and silver (al-hajarān). Imam Abu Hanifa held that the original owner's right is not cut off, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagreed. This lesson unpacks the key arguments and the practical consequences of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Articulate Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling: the usurper does not own gold or silver even after making them into vessels, coins, or jewelry. The original owner can take them back without compensation.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the usurper becomes owner because valuable craftsmanship was added. They analogize to iron or brass: if a usurper makes iron into a vessel, he owns it.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Imam Abu Hanifa responds that gold and silver retain their essential nature (thumuniyya) – they are still sold by weight, riba applies, and the name 'gold' or 'silver' remains. Hence, the object is not consumed in any respect.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Imam's view, the original owner can reclaim the transformed gold/silver for free. Under the Sahibayn, the usurper owns it and must pay the value (badal) – or the owner must pay for the craftsmanship.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi madhhab follows Imam Abu Hanifa's position as the stronger one, since the nature of gold/silver as price remains unchanged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الغصب

وشي وزرع واتخاذ سيف أو أناء لغير الحجرين وبناء على ساجة ولو ذبح شاة أو خرق

قال رحمه الله : (وملك بلا حل انتفاع قبل أداء الضمان بطحن وطبخ وشي وزرع واتخاذ سيف أو أناء لغير الحجرين) لأنه لو لم يملكه بذلك لحقه ضرر وكان ظلماً والظالم لا يظلم بل ينصف. ثم الضابط فيه أنه متى تغيرت العين المغصوبة بفعل حتى زال اسمها وعظم منافعها واختلطت بملك الغاصب حتى لا يمكن تميزها أصلاً زال ملك المغصوب منه وملكها الغاصب وضمنها ولا يحل له الانتفاع بها حتى يؤدي بدلها قال في العناية وغيرها : وقوله بطحن إلى آخره يعني بفعل الغاصب احترازاً عما إذا تغير بغير فعله مثل إن صار العنب زبيباً بنفسه أو خلاً أو الرطب تمراً فإن الغاصب لا يملكه والمالك فيه بالخيار إن شاء أخذه وإن شاء تركه وضمنه مثله. وقوله زال اسمها يحترز عما إذا لم يزل اسمها كما لو ذبح الشاة فإنه يقال شاة حية وشاة مذبوحة. وقوله عظم منافعها تأكيد يتناول الحنطة إذا طحنها فإنه يزول بالطحن عظم منافعها كجعلها هريسة وكشكاً ونشاء وغير ذلك. قال صاحب العناية : وقوله وعظم منافعها تأكيد لقوله زال اسمها والظاهر أنه تأسيس لا تأكيد لأنه احتراز عما إذا غصب شاة وذبحها فإنه لا يزول بالذبح ملك مالكها كما سيأتي مصرحاً به، وما ذكره ره من الطحن وما بعده يحصل به ما ذكرنا في الضابط فيملكها الغاصب إلا الذهب والفضة فإنه لا يملكه باتخاذهما أواني أو دراهم أو دنانير عند الإمام لأنها بهذا الفعل لا يزول التمييز. وقال الإمام الشافعي : لا ينقطع حق المالك بما ذكر وهي رواية عن أبي يوسف غير أنه إذا أختار أخذ العين لا يضمن النقصان في الربويات لأن الملك نعمة فلا يحصل بالحرام وهو الغصب وصار كما وقعت الحنطة في الطاحونة وانطحنت بفعل الماء أو الهواء من غير صنع أحد. ولنا ان لما استهلك العين من وجه بالاستحالة حتى صار له اسم آخر وقد أحدث وهي حق الغا سب وهي قائمة من كل وجه فترجحت لذلك والمحظور لغيره لا يمتنع أن يكون سبباً لحكم شرعي ألا ترى أن الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة لا تجوز وتكون سبباً لحصول الثواب ا زيل فما ظنك بالملك غير أنه لا يجوز له الانتفاع بها قبل الأداء لا ينفتح باب الغصب ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في الشاة المذبوحة بغير إذن مالكها «أطعموها الأسارى ولو لم يملكه لما قال ذلك والقياس أنه يجوز الانتفاع به وهو قول الحسن زفر ورواية عن أبي حنيفة ولهذا ينفذ تصرفه فيها كالتمليك للغير. ووجه الاستحسان ما ذكرناه ونفاذ تصرفه لوجود الملك ألا ترى أن المشتري شراء فاسداً ينفذ تصرفه فيه مع أنه لا يحل له الانتفاع به. فإذا دفع المثل أو القيمة إليه وأخذه بحكم الحاكم أو تراضيا على مقدار حل الانتفاع به لوجود الرضا من المغصوب منه لأن الحاكم لا يحكم إلا بطلبه فحصلت المبادلة بالتراضي. وقال أبو يوسف في الحنطة المزروعة والنواة المزروعة يجوز الانتفاع بها قبل أداء الضمان لوجود الاستهلاك من كل وجه . وقيد بقوله واتخاذ سيف ليفيد أنه بعده صار يباع فيه الصنعة

كان عدداً لا وزناً وهو إنما يملكه بما ذكر من الاتخاذ إذا كان يباع عدداً. وفي المحيط : ولو غصب حديداً وصفراً فجعله إناء فإن كان يباع وزناً لا ينقطع حق المالك كما في الفضة، وإن عدداً يباع انقطع حق المالك لأنه لما أخرجه عن كونه موزوناً يكون مستهلكاً له من وجه . قال في شرح الطحاوي : وقال شمس الأئمة الكرخي : الصحيح أنه لا فرق بين الصفقة أن يباع عدداً أو وزناً ولو غصب فلوساً وضاع منها إناء ضمن الفلوس لأنه أخرجها عن كونها ثمناً فيصير مستهلكاً من وجه وقوله لغير الحجرين يعني أن الحجرين لو اتخذ مصاغاً أو حلياً أو إناء أو ضربه دراهم أو دنانير فللمالك أن يأخذه ولا يعطيه شيئاً عند الإمام، وعندهما هو للغاصب ويضمن مثله للمالك لأنه أحدث فيه صنعة متقومة فصار كما لو غصب حديداً أو صفراً فضربه. وللإمام أن العين باقية من كل وجه ولم تهلك من وجه ما ألا ترى أن الاسم لم يتغير ومعناه الثمنية وهو باقي أيضاً. وكذا كونه موزوناً باقٍ أيضاً حتى يجري فيه الربا. وأطلق في الحجرين شمل ما إذا صار بعد الاتخاذ أصلاً أو تبعاً. قال في المحيط : ولو غصب فضة أو دراهم فجعلها عروة أو قلادة لا أواني انقطع حق المالك لأنه صار تبعاً للأواني والتبعية استهلاك من وجه اهـ .

ماء
وفي فتاوي سمرقند : غصب من آخر طعاماً فمضغه حتى صار بالمضغ مستهلكاً فلما ابتلعه كان حلالاً في قول الإمام وقالا : لا يكون حلالاً إلا إذا أدى البدل. وأنكر الشيخ الإمام نجم الدين النسفي هذه الرواية عن الإمام وقال الصحيح أن قول الإمام كقولهما . وفي الخانية وقولهما احتياط .اهـ. وفي المنتقى عن أبي يوسف : لو غصب أرضاً وبنى فيها حوانيت ومسجداً وحماماً فلا بأس بالصلاة في ذلك المسجد، وأما الحمام فلا يدخل ولا تستأجر الحوانيت. وقال هشام أنا أكره الصلاة فيه حتى يطيب اربابه وأكره شراء المتاع من أرض غصب أو حوانيت غصب .اهـ. وأشار المؤلف إلى أن التغيير بعدما وضع اليد في المثلي فلو كان قبله تجب القيمة . قال القدوري : صب ماء في طعام فأفسده وزاد في كيله فلصاحب الطعام أن يضمنه قيمته قبل أن يصب فيه الماء وليس له أن يضمنه مثله، وكذا لو صب في دهن أو زيت لا يجوز أن يغرم مثل كيله قبل صب الماء لأنه لم يكن منه غصب متقدم حتى لو غصب ثم صب الماء فعليه مثله .اهـ. وفي الذخيرة وإن باع رجل شيئاً ثم إن البائع فعل بعض ما وصفنا فكل شيء كان الغاصب فيه مستهلكاً للعين ولم يكن للمغصوب منه أن يأخذه فكذا ليس للمشتري أن يأخذه وكل شيء لم يكن الغاصب فيه مستهلكاً وكان للمغصوب منه أن يأخذه فللمشتري أن يأخذه .اهـ. وفي الفتاوى : لو غصب حنطة فاتخذها كشكاً فلصاحبها أخذها ورد ما زاد فيها من اللبن واستشكله بعض أهل العصر وهو الصحيح لأنه زال اسمها وعظم منافعها وأجيب بأن المراد إذا سقى الحنطة اللبن من غير طحن أما إذا طحنها فقد ملكها ويرد مثلها . قال رحمه الله : ( وبناء على ساجة) يعني إذا بنى على السامجة البحر الرائق ج ٨/ م١٤
Book of Usurpation. Roasting and planting and taking a sword or a vessel for other than the two stones, and building on a plank, and if he slaughtered a sheep or tore. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: And he owns without permissible benefit before paying the guarantee, by grinding, cooking, roasting, planting, taking a sword or a vessel for other than the two stones. Because if he did not own it thereby, harm would befall him and it would be oppression, and the oppressor is not oppressed but receives justice. Then the criterion thereof is that whenever the usurped object changes by an act until its name disappears and its benefits become great and it becomes mixed with the property of the usurper such that it cannot be distinguished at all, the ownership of the person from whom it was usurped ceases and the usurper owns it and guarantees it, and it is not permissible for him to benefit from it until he pays its substitute. It was said in al-Inayah and others: His statement 'by grinding' etc. means by the act of the usurper, as a precaution against when it changes without his act, such as if grapes become raisins by themselves or vinegar, or fresh dates become dry dates, for then the usurper does not own it, and the owner has the choice: if he wishes, he takes it, and if he wishes, he leaves it and guarantees its equivalent. His statement 'its name disappeared' guards against when its name does not disappear, as when a sheep is slaughtered, for it is said 'live sheep' and 'slaughtered sheep'. His statement 'its benefits became great' is a confirmation that includes wheat when ground, for by grinding its great benefits disappear, like making it into harisah, kashk, starch, etc. The author of al-Inayah said: His statement 'and its benefits became great' is a confirmation of his statement 'its name disappeared', and apparently it is an establishment (ta'sis) not a confirmation, because it guards against when he usurped a sheep and slaughtered it, for slaughter does not remove the ownership of its owner as will be explicitly stated later. And what he mentioned of grinding and thereafter achieves what we mentioned in the criterion, so the usurper owns it except gold and silver, for he does not own it by making them into vessels or dirhams or dinars according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) because by this act the distinction does not disappear. Al-Imam al-Shafi'i said: The right of the owner is not cut off by what is mentioned, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf that if he chooses to take the object, he does not guarantee the deficiency in ribawi items because ownership is a blessing and thus is not acquired by something unlawful, i.e., usurpation, and it becomes like wheat that falls into a mill and is ground by the action of water or wind without anyone's doing. And for us: since he has consumed the object in one respect by transformation until it has another name and he has created (value), and it is the right of the usurper, and it exists in every respect, so it is preponderant for that reason. And a prohibition due to something else does not prevent being a cause for a legal ruling. Do you not see that prayer in usurped land is not permitted and is a cause for obtaining reward? So what about ownership? However, it is not permissible for him to benefit from it before payment, so that the door of usurpation is not opened, and because of his statement, peace be upon him, regarding the slaughtered sheep without the permission of its owner: 'Feed it to the captives.' If he did not own it, he would not have said that. And by analogy (qiyas) it is permissible to benefit from it, and that is the saying of Hasan al-Zafar and a narration from Abu Hanifa, and thus his disposal in it is effective, like giving ownership to another. And the basis of istihsan is what we mentioned, and the effectiveness of his disposal is due to the existence of ownership. Do you not see that a buyer in a void purchase (fāsid) has effective disposal in it even though it is not permissible for him to benefit from it? So when he pays the equivalent or the value to him, and takes it by the judgment of a judge or they mutually agree on an amount, then benefiting from it becomes permissible due to the existence of consent from the usurped owner, because the judge only judges upon his request, so an exchange by mutual consent is achieved. Abu Yusuf said regarding planted wheat and planted date-pit: it is permissible to benefit from them before paying the guarantee because consumption exists in every respect. And he restricted by his statement 'taking a sword' to indicate that after that, it becomes sold for the craftsmanship. It was number not weight, and he only owns it by the mentioned making if it is sold by number. In al-Muhit: If he usurped iron and brass and made them into a vessel, if it is sold by weight, the owner's right is not cut off as with silver, but if sold by number, the owner's right is cut off because by removing it from being a weight item, he has consumed it in one respect. In Sharh al-Tahawi: Shams al-A'imma al-Karkhi said: The correct is that there is no difference whether the item is sold by number or weight. If he usurped fulus (copper coins) and made from them a vessel, he guarantees the fulus because he has removed them from being a price, so it becomes consumed in one respect. His statement 'for other than the two stones' means that if he made the two stones into jewelry or ornaments or a vessel, or struck them into dirhams or dinars, the owner may take it and give nothing according to Imam. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it belongs to the usurper, and he guarantees its equivalent to the owner because he has created valuable craftsmanship in it, so it is like if he usurped iron or brass and struck it. For Imam (Abu Hanifa), the object remains in every respect and has not perished in any respect. Do you not see that the name has not changed and its meaning as a price also remains, and likewise its being sold by weight remains such that riba applies to it. He made it general in 'the two stones' to include whether after making it becomes an original or a dependent. In al-Muhit: If he usurped silver or dirhams and made them into a handle or a necklace, not a vessel, the owner's right is cut off because it has become a dependent of the vessel, and dependentship is consumption in one respect. In Fatawa Samarqand: Someone usurped food from another and chewed it until it became consumed by chewing, then when he swallowed it, it was halal according to Imam. The two said: It is not halal unless he pays the substitute. Shaykh al-Imam Najm al-Din al-Nasafi denied this narration from Imam and said the correct is that the saying of Imam is like their saying. In al-Khaniyya: and their saying is precautionary. In al-Muntaqa from Abu Yusuf: If he usurped land and built shops, a mosque, and a bathhouse, there is no harm in praying in that mosque, but as for the bathhouse, he should not enter, and the shops should not be rented. Hisham said: I dislike prayer in it until its owners become pleased, and I dislike buying goods from usurped land or usurped shops. The author indicated that the change is after taking possession in the case of a fungible (mithli). If before, the value is owed. Al-Quduri said: He poured water into food, spoiling it and increasing its measure, so the owner of the food may guarantee its value before the water was poured, and he may not guarantee its equivalent. Likewise, if he poured into oil or sesame oil, he may not owe the like of its measure before pouring water because there was no prior usurpation. If he usurped and then poured water, then he owes its equivalent. In al-Dhakhira: If a man sold something, then the seller did some of what we described, then everything in which the usurper consumed the object and the usurped owner could not take it, likewise the buyer cannot take it. And everything in which the usurper was not a consumer and the usurped owner could take it, the buyer may take it. In al-Fatawa: If he usurped wheat and made it into kashk, its owner may take it and return the milk added to it, and some contemporaries considered it problematic, and it is correct because its name disappeared and its benefits became great. It was answered that the intended meaning is if he watered the wheat with milk without grinding; but if he ground it, then he has owned it and returns its like. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And building on a plank) means if he built on the plank (sajjah).
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe (sharh) of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the topic of ghasp (usurpation). The author, Imam Ibn Nujaym, explains the ruling that when a usurper transforms the usurped object through his own action (such as grinding, cooking, etc.) such that its original name changes, its benefits greatly increase, and it becomes inseparably mixed with the usurper's property, the usurper becomes the owner of the transformed object, but he is not permitted to benefit from it until he pays the substitute (badal) to the original owner. This is based on the principle that the usurper should not be left at a loss, but also should not profit from his wrong. The criterion is carefully defined: the change must be by the usurper's act (not natural), the name must disappear (so slaughter does not suffice since the name 'sheep' remains), and benefits must greatly increase. The author then discusses exceptions: gold and silver (the 'two stones') – according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the original owner retains ownership even if the usurper makes them into vessels or coins because their essential nature as a medium of exchange and their quality of being sold by weight remains; thus the owner can take them back without compensation. However, the two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybai, hold that the usurper owns them and must pay the value, since valuable craftsmanship has been added. Al-Shafi'i is also cited as denying any transfer of ownership at all. The passage then addresses related subsidiary issues: the case of planting seeds, building on land, chewing food, making a vessel from copper coins, and the effect on buyers. The overall thrust is to balance the rights of the owner with practical necessity, ensuring that the usurper is held liable but not unjustly burdened.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasp): Usurpation: taking another's property without right, with the potential for ownership transfer upon transformation.
حجران (hajarān): Literally 'two stones', meaning gold and silver (the two precious metals used as currency).
بدل (badal): Substitute or compensation: the equivalent (mithl) for fungibles or value (qīmah) for non-fungibles that the usurper must pay to the owner.
ثمنية (thumuniyya): The quality of being a price or medium of exchange, characteristic of gold and silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens to gold that a usurper melts and makes into a ring?
A) The usurper owns it and must pay its value.
B) The original owner may take it back without paying anything.
C) The usurper owns it and may use it immediately.
D) The ring becomes the property of the state.

Key Takeaway
Under the Hanafi madhhab, gold and silver are unique: even after transformation, the original owner's right persists, unlike other materials.

Usurping Iron or Brass and Making a Vessel: Weight vs Count
Ruling on change of form in usurped property and its effect on ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a usurper acquires ownership of transformed goods based on market practice (weight vs count) and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute involving al-Karkhi.

Core Idea
Change of form severs original ownership only if the item is sold by count, not by weight.

This passage from al-Muhit and Sharh al-Tahawi addresses a key question in Hanafi property law: when does transforming usurped material transfer ownership to the usurper? The answer depends not on the material itself but on how it is customarily sold—by weight or by count. Understanding this distinction is essential for determining whether the original owner can reclaim the item or must accept compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
Identify who did what: the usurper (ghāṣib) took iron or brass (ḥadīd or ṣufr) and made it into a vessel (inā’). The original owner (mālik) claims the vessel or compensation.
The act is a change of form (taghyīr al-‘ayn), not mere use.
2
State the ruling based on sale method
If the material is sold by weight (waznan), the owner's right remains—the usurper does not own the vessel. If sold by count (ʿaddan), the owner's right is cut off—the usurper owns the vessel but must pay its value.
This distinction is from al-Muhit, considered the relied-upon (muftā bihī) position.
3
Identify the proof (dalīl)
The ruling is based on qiyās (analogy) to silver (fiḍḍa), which is always sold by weight. Changing silver's form does not sever ownership because the substance remains identifiable. For count-based items, changing form is considered istihlāk min wajh (partial consumption), which terminates the original claim.
The 'illa (effective cause) is the mode of sale, not the material itself.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam al-Karkhī (Shams al-A’imma) disagreed, holding that there is no difference between weight and count—transformation severs ownership in both cases. This view is recorded in Sharh al-Tahawī.
Al-Karkhī's opinion is noted but not adopted as the muftā bihī.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf)
Under the majority view, if the material is weight-based (e.g., iron sold by weight), the owner can reclaim the vessel. If count-based (e.g., brass sold by count), the owner must accept compensation. Under al-Karkhī's view, the owner always loses the right to the specific item.
This difference affects whether the remedy is specific performance (return of 'ayn) or damages (qīmah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان عدداً لا وزناً وهو إنما يملكه بما ذكر من الاتخاذ إذا كان يباع عدداً. وفي المحيط : ولو غصب حديداً وصفراً فجعله إناء فإن كان يباع وزناً لا ينقطع حق المالك كما في الفضة، وإن عدداً يباع انقطع حق المالك لأنه لما أخرجه عن كونه موزوناً يكون مستهلكاً له من وجه . قال في شرح الطحاوي : وقال شمس الأئمة الكرخي : الصحيح أنه لا فرق بين الصفقة أن يباع عدداً أو وزناً
It was (sold) by count, not by weight, and he only owns it by the mentioned making if it is sold by count. In al-Muhit: If someone usurped iron or brass and made it into a vessel, if it is sold by weight, the owner's right is not cut off, as in silver; if sold by count, the owner's right is cut off, because by removing it from being weight-based he has consumed it in one respect. He said in Sharh al-Tahawi: Shams al-A'imma al-Karkhi said: The correct view is that there is no difference between a transaction being sold by count or by weight.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author of al-Muhit distinguishes between materials sold by weight (like silver) and those sold by count. Changing the form of a weight-based material does not sever the original owner's ownership because the substance (ayn) remains identifiable. However, changing a count-based material's form is considered partial consumption (istihlak min wajh), terminating the owner's claim. Imam al-Karkhi rejects this distinction, holding that regardless of sale method, the transformation severs ownership. The Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah supports al-Muhit's distinction, but al-Karkhi's view is also noted. The practical effect: in a weight-based item, the usurper owes the same item; in count-based, he owes its value.

Key Terms
استهلاك من وجه (istihlak min wajh): Partial consumption where the original item's identity is lost in one aspect (e.g., form) but remains in another (e.g., substance), leading to transfer of ownership.
موزون (mawzūn): An item sold by weight in the market.
معدود (maʿdūd): An item sold by count in the market.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (al-Muhit), what happens to the owner's right when someone usurps brass (sold by count) and makes it into a vessel?
A) The owner can reclaim the vessel without compensation.
B) The owner's right is cut off, and the usurper owns the vessel.
C) The owner can reclaim the vessel but must pay the value of the work.
D) The owner's right remains, and the usurper must return the brass in its original form.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, whether a usurper acquires ownership of transformed goods depends on market custom: if sold by weight, owner retains right; if by count, owner loses right.

Usurping Fulus and Transformation into a Vessel
Ruling on usurping coins and transforming them into a vessel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when fulus are transformed into a vessel and explain why the transformation is considered partial consumption (istihlak min wajh) due to loss of thamaniyyah.

Core Idea
Changing fulus from currency to a vessel makes the usurper liable because the character of thamaniyyah is lost.

In this lesson we examine a specific case of usurpation (ghasb) involving fulus (copper coins). The key legal question is: what happens when the usurper transforms the coins into a different object, such as a vessel? The Hanafi ruling hinges on the nature of fulus as thaman (currency). We will see that the transformation severs ownership and triggers liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is usurping fulus and making them into a vessel. The ruling: the usurper is liable for the value of the fulus (not the vessel).
2
Understand the key concept: thamaniyyah
Fulus are considered thaman (currency). Their primary function is to serve as a medium of exchange. This characteristic is called thamaniyyah.
Thamaniyyah is a legal attribute that affects rulings on ownership and liability.
3
Apply the principle: loss of thamaniyyah is consumption
By making a vessel, the fulus lose their character as currency. This is considered istihlak min wajh (partial consumption) because the substance remains but the intended use is destroyed.
The Hanafi school treats this as equivalent to consuming the value.
4
Determine the liability
Since the fulus are no longer in their original form as currency, the usurper must compensate the owner with the market value of the fulus at the time of usurpation.
The owner does not receive the vessel; he receives the value of the coins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو غصب فلوساً وضاع منها إناء ضمن الفلوس لأنه أخرجها عن كونها ثمناً فيصير مستهلكاً من وجه
And if someone usurped fulus and made from them a vessel, he is liable for the fulus because he removed them from being currency, so he becomes a consumer in one respect.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This is a ruling statement: usurping fulus (copper coins used as currency) and making them into a vessel terminates the original owner's ownership. The reason is that fulus are primarily currency (thaman); changing them into a vessel removes their character as a medium of exchange, which is considered partial consumption (istihlak min wajh). Therefore, the usurper is liable to pay the value of the fulus (not the vessel) to the owner. This is consistent with the earlier principle that changing a countable item's form severs ownership.

Key Terms
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins used as currency in classical Islamic markets; considered thaman (price) by nature.
ثمناً (thaman): Currency; what serves as a medium of exchange and measure of value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the usurper of fulus liable when he makes them into a vessel?
A) Because he destroyed the physical substance of the fulus.
B) Because he removed the fulus from being currency (thaman).
C) Because the vessel is worth more than the fulus.
D) Because the owner did not consent to the transformation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that usurping fulus and transforming them into a vessel severs the original owner's ownership, making the usurper liable for the value of the fulus because the transformation destroys their character as currency (thamaniyyah).

Imam vs Sahibayn: Reclaiming Transformed Gold and Silver
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ownership after transformation of gold and silver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on ownership of gold/silver transformed by a usurper and explain the basis (dalil) for each position.

Core Idea
Gold and silver remain the owner's property even after transformation because their substance and currency nature persist.

In Hanafi fiqh, the transformation of gold and silver into different forms—such as jewelry or coins—raises a nuanced ownership question. This lesson explores the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding whether the original owner can reclaim the transformed object without compensation. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between changes in form and changes in legal identity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The issue is whether a usurper who transforms another's gold or silver into a new form (e.g., necklace, coin) acquires ownership of the resulting object.
The base matn excludes gold/silver from the general rule that the usurper owns the transformed object.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Imam holds that the owner can reclaim the object without compensating the usurper. His proof: the substance (ayn) remains entirely unchanged—the name 'gold' or 'silver' persists, the function as currency (thamaniyyah) remains, and riba still applies to it.
Note the use of 'al-ayn baqiyah' (the substance remains).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn hold that the usurper owns the new object and must pay the owner its like (mithl). Their proof: the workmanship (sin'ah mutaqawwimah) adds value and effectively creates a new property, analogous to transforming iron or brass.
The analogy to iron/brass is key—these materials do not have the same special status as gold/silver.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
Imam's reasoning is considered stronger because the change is only in form, not in the legal essence of the material. The continuity of riba and weight-based measurement confirms that the substance has not been consumed.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view is Imam Abu Hanifa's.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Imam's view, the owner reclaims the object free of charge; under the Sahibayn's view, the owner receives monetary compensation and loses the object.
This difference affects both ownership rights and potential disputes in transactions involving precious metals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله لغير الحجرين يعني أن الحجرين لو اتخذ مصاغاً أو حلياً أو إناء أو ضربه دراهم أو دنانير فللمالك أن يأخذه ولا يعطيه شيئاً عند الإمام، وعندهما هو للغاصب ويضمن مثله للمالك لأنه أحدث فيه صنعة متقومة فصار كما لو غصب حديداً أو صفراً فضربه. وللإمام أن العين باقية من كل وجه ولم تهلك من وجه ما ألا ترى أن الاسم لم يتغير ومعناه الثمنية وهو باقي أيضاً. وكذا كونه موزوناً باقٍ أيضاً حتى يجري فيه الربا.
And his saying 'other than the two stones' means that if the two stones are made into jewelry, ornament, or vessel, or struck into dirhams or dinars, then according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) the owner may take it and give nothing; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it belongs to the usurper and he must pay its like to the owner because he produced a valuable workmanship, so it is as if he usurped iron or brass and struck it. And for Imam, the substance remains in every respect and has not perished in any respect; do you not see that the name has not changed and its meaning of being currency remains as well. Similarly, being weight-based remains, so that riba applies to it.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Imam vs Sahibayn) regarding the transformation of gold and silver (the two stones) from raw form into jewelry, coins, or vessels. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the original owner can reclaim the transformed object without paying anything, because the substance (ayn) remains entirely intact—the name 'gold' or 'silver' hasn't changed, and its function as currency (thamaniyyah) persists. Thus, no partial consumption occurred. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the valuable workmanship (sin'ah) added by the usurper constitutes a separate property right, so the usurper owns the object and must pay the owner its weight equivalent (mithl). Imam supports his position by noting that riba (usury) still applies to the metal, confirming its unchanged nature. The term 'other than the two stones' refers to an exception in the matn: for gold/silver, the ruling differs from other materials. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as it is the stronger proof based on the continuity of the substance.

Key Terms
الحجرين (al-hajarayn): The two stones: gold and silver in their raw state, before being worked into coins or jewelry.
صنعة متقومة (sin'ah mutaqawwimah): Valuable workmanship that adds economic value to the material.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens when a usurper makes gold dust into a necklace?
A) The owner can reclaim the necklace without paying anything.
B) The owner can reclaim the necklace but must pay for the workmanship.
C) The usurper owns the necklace and must pay the value of the gold.
D) The usurper can keep the necklace without compensation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, gold and silver retain their legal identity even after transformation, so the original owner can reclaim them from a usurper without compensation.

Owner's Options When Usurped Property Is Altered by Building or Planting
Commentary on building, planting, and plastering on usurped property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when a usurper builds on land or inserts a plank into a building, and apply the valuation principle to determine the owner's options.

Core Idea
When a usurper adds value to property, the owner may either take the property and compensate the increase, or leave it and claim full value.

Usurpation (ghasb) often involves the usurper adding to or altering the property—building on land, planting trees, or inserting materials. The Hanafi school balances the rights of the original owner with the reality of transformation. This lesson examines the key rule: when the added value exceeds the original property's value, the owner loses the right to reclaim the property and instead must accept compensation; otherwise, the owner may take the property and pay for the increase. We will follow the commentator's analysis of various scenarios from the texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the changed property and the increase
Determine what the usurper did (building, planting, plastering) and whether the added value is greater than the original property's value. This determines who 'owns' the composite.
The comparison is between the value of the original item (e.g., plank, land) and the total value after addition.
2
Apply the 'greater value' rule
If the building's value exceeds the land's, the owner cannot take the land; he must take its value. If the plank's value exceeds the building's, the owner can reclaim the plank.
This is the majority view; there is also a minority view that if building on a plank itself (not around it), the owner can demolish.
3
Consider the nature of the addition
If the usurper builds with material from the land itself (e.g., soil), the wall belongs to the landowner; if with foreign material, the usurper may demolish or be compensated.
This applies to walls built on usurped land.
4
Examine the effect of a judge's ruling
If the judge has already ordered the usurper to pay the value, the usurper may not demolish the building; otherwise, mashayikh differed on permissibility.
The ruling aims to avoid wasteful destruction.
5
Apply the gift/discharge principle
If the usurper gifts the altered property or the owner gifts it to the usurper, it counts as a discharge of liability for the usurpation.
The gift is valid because it effectively releases the usurper from the obligation to return the specific item.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بعض العين وبعض المنفعة واليسير مما لا يفوت به شيء من المنفعة وإنما تفوت الجودة. قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : القطع أنواع ثلاثة : فاحش غير مستأصل وهو ما بينا، وقطع يسير وهو أن يقطع طرفاً من أطراف الثوب ولا يثبت فيه الخيار للمالك ولكن يضمنه النقصان وقطع فاحش مستأصل للثوب وهو أن يقطع الثوب قطعاً لا يصلح لما يراد منه ولا يرغب في شرائه؛ فعن الإمام المالك بالخيار إن شاء ترك المقطوع وضمنه القيمة وإن شاء أخذ المقطوع ولا شيء له.
Book of Usurpation. The owner's ownership ceased over it, and the expression is absolute so it includes whether the value of the plank is more or the value of the building. And he said in al-Dhakhira: This is when the value of the building is more than the value of the plank. But if the value of the plank is more than the value of the building, then he does not own it and he has the right to take it. And it is apparent from the restriction of building on the plank that if he built on land that cannot be imagined to be usurped, he does not own it. And in al-Mudmarat: If he usurped land and built on it and the value of the building is more than the value of the land, the usurped-from has no way to the land, and the usurper guarantees the value of his land, and thus it is narrated from Abu al-Qasim al-Dabbasi. And in al-Hawi: He usurped from another a house or land and built a building or planted, then the owner uprooted the plant and demolished the building, he is not liable provided he does not break the wood or brick of the usurper. And in al-Asl: He usurped land and built on it, then the owner came and took the land, and the usurper wanted to take the wall. If the usurper built the wall from the soil of that land, he has no right to demolish, and the wall belongs to the owner. If he built the wall not from the soil of that land, he has the right to demolish. And in Fatawa Samarqand: A man built a wall in another's vineyard from the soil of his vineyard without his permission. If the soil has no value, it belongs to the owner. If the soil has value, the wall belongs to the builder and he owes the value of the building. End. And he did not mention in al-Asl whether if the usurper wants to demolish the building and return the plank, is that permissible for him? This has two aspects: If the judge ruled against him for the value, it is not permissible for him, and if he demolishes, he cannot return the building. If the judge did not rule against him for the value, the mashayikh differed: Some said he does not own the right to demolish, some said it is not permissible for him due to wasting wealth without benefit. And in Fatawa al-Nasafi: He was asked about one who usurped a plank and inserted it into his building, or a sapling and planted it in his land, or a branch and attached it to a tree, then the usurper gifted it to the usurped-from, does he become free from liability by this gift? He said: Yes. It was said: And if the usurped-from said to the usurper, 'I gift you the plank or the sapling or the branch'? He said: Yes. It was said: How, when the usurped-from gifted to the usurper what he does not own, because his right has ceased due to liability on the usurper? He said: Yes, and this in meaning is a discharge from the liability required on him for this specific item. And in al-Khaniyya: He broke another's branch, he guarantees the deficiency, even if the break was excessive such that it became firewood or a peg. And in al-Asl: He usurped another's house and painted it for ten thousand, then the owner came, it was said to him: If you wish, take the house and give the usurper what he added to it. And in al-Dhakhira: The buyer of the house from the usurper, if he demolished it and inserted it into his building, then the owner appeared: if the building was little and its removal was easy, he removes it and returns it to the owner; if it was much and its removal was difficult, and if he wishes he does not remove it but leaves it and the buyer guarantees the value of the first building. And in al-Quduri: If he usurped another's house and plastered it, then returned it, it was said to its owner: Give what the plastering increased, unless the owner is pleased that the usurper take what he plastered. Hisham said: I said to Muhammad concerning a man who took possession of a door that had been removed and painted it with fingers: He said: Its way is the way of the house. I said: And if he painted it by carving and not with fingers? He said: Then this is wealth consumed with the door, and it became obligatory due to... A garment excessively torn: he guarantees the value and hands over the usurped item, or guarantees the deficiency. And for a slight tear, he guarantees the deficiency and pays its value, and the door is his. Similarly, if he carved a silver vessel by carving. And al-Karkhi mentioned that it is based on the issue of the plank: if the usurper built around the plank, but if he built on the plank itself, the owner's ownership is not voided, rather he demolishes it. And this is the choice of Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, because if he built around it, he was not transgressing, and if he built on it, he was transgressing. And the correct view is that the answer in both places is the same; thus in al-Bada'i. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he slaughters a sheep or tears a garment excessively, he guarantees the value and hands over the usurped item or guarantees the deficiency. Similarly, if he slaughters and cuts the hand or foot, because these things are destruction in one sense due to loss of some purposes like carrying, house, and offspring, and loss of some benefit in the garment. So the owner chooses between demanding full value and leaving it to him, and between demanding the deficiency and taking it. And al-Hasan reported from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that he cannot demand the deficiency if he takes the meat, because slaughter and skinning are an increase since the possibility of dying naturally is cut off, and benefit from its meat becomes possible and determined. The first opinion is the apparent one because it is a deficiency in terms of loss of some purposes as we explained. And if the animal is not edible flesh, the cutter of the limb guarantees its full value because it is consumption in every respect, unlike cutting a limb, because after cutting it is suitable for all purposes it was suitable for before. And that is not the same for the animal, because it becomes unfit for carrying or riding after cutting. He restricts the choice to slaughtering a sheep and what is eaten for its flesh to exclude what is not eaten for its flesh. He said in al-Khaniyya: If he slaughtered another's donkey, then according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) he cannot guarantee the deficiency, but he guarantees full value. And according to Muhammad, he may keep the donkey and guarantee the deficiency, or if he wishes, he guarantees full value and does not keep the donkey. If he kills it by killing, it is based on the previous difference, and reliance is on the saying of the Imam. And if he cuts the hand of a donkey or a mule, or cuts its leg, or gouges out its eye, the Imam said: If he wishes, he delivers the body and guarantees full value, and he cannot keep the body and guarantee the deficiency. And in al-Muntaqa, Hisham from Muhammad: A man cut the hand of a donkey or a mule or its leg, and what remained had value, then he may keep it and take the deficiency. And in al-Nawazil: If he cuts the ear of an animal or part of it, he guarantees the deficiency. If he cuts both ears, he guarantees the deficiency. And from his teacher, may Allah be pleased with him: If he cuts the tail of the qadi's donkey, he guarantees its full value; if it is another's, he guarantees the deficiency. End. I say: The donkey of the mufti, the scholar, and the amir are attached to the donkey of the qadi. And in al-Tajrid: The correct distinction between excessive tearing and slight tearing is that excessive tearing is that by which some of the substance and some of the benefit are lost, and slight is that by which no benefit is lost, only the quality is lost. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: Cutting is of three types: Excessive but not destructive, which is what we have explained; Slight cutting, which is to cut a part of the edges of the garment, and the owner does not have a choice in it, but he guarantees the deficiency; Excessive and destructive cutting of the garment, which is to cut the garment in such a way that it is not suitable for its intended purpose and no one desires to buy it. For that, the owner (Imam) has the choice: if he wishes, he leaves the cut garment and guarantees its value, and if he wishes, he takes the cut garment and gets nothing.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on rulings of usurpation (ghasb) where the usurper alters the property. The commentator draws from multiple sources including al-Asl, Fatawa, and later works, presenting various scenarios and the Hanafi positions with intra-madhhab differences.

The text first discusses building on usurped land: if the value of the building is greater than the land, the usurper may own the land and compensate the owner; if the value of the plank (building material) is greater, the owner may take it back. The principle is that ownership of the usurped item may transfer to the usurper due to the increase in value, but the original owner has a choice based on valuation.

Then it covers cases of planting, plastering, and constructing walls, with rulings depending on whether the materials came from the usurped property or elsewhere. The involvement of a judge's ruling affects whether the usurper can demolish the building.

Next, the text addresses gifts from the usurper to the original owner as a discharge of liability. It also discusses breaking branches and painting houses, where the owner is compensated for increase in value.

A key part is the distinction between excessive and slight damage to a garment or animal. For excessive damage, the owner can choose to take the item and claim full value, or keep the item and claim only the reduction in value. For slight damage, only the deficiency is compensated. The commentator explores various subcases: slaughtering an edible animal vs. an inedible one (like a donkey), cutting limbs, and the definitions of excessive tearing. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding whether the owner can claim only the deficiency when the item (like a slaughtered sheep) can still be used for meat.

The passage concludes with a classification by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani of three types of cutting: excessive but not destructive, slight, and excessive and destructive, each with its own ruling.

Throughout, the commentary maintains the Hanafi framework, citing authoritative works and resolving differences.

Key Terms
خرق فاحش (kharq fāḥish): Excessive tearing that destroys the utility of the garment or reduces its value significantly.
نقصان (nuqṣān): The reduction in value of an item due to damage or change.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi position, if a usurper slaughters another's sheep, what options does the owner have?
A) The owner must take the meat and claim full value.
B) The owner may either take the meat and claim the deficiency or leave the meat and claim full value.
C) The owner can only claim the value of the meat, not the live animal.
D) The owner has no recourse because the animal is dead.

Key Takeaway
When a usurper excessively damages property, the owner can choose between taking the damaged item and claiming the deficiency, or leaving it and claiming full value.
